Conversation &

Conversation is informal talk between one or more people. There are currently
two schools of thought: the direct approach, and the indirect approach. The
former argues that the characteristic features of conversation, as identified in
conversation analysis, should 66 taught explicitly and 10 isolation, before being
integrated into freer practice activities. The indirect approach, on the other hand,
argues that conversation is best learned by having conversations. Accordingly,
the conversation syllabus might consist of a list of topics or of situations where

conversations are likely to occur.

대 화 는 주 로 한 사 람 이 상 이 나 눈 비 공 식 적 인 발 화 를 말 한 다 . 명 시 적 인 대 화 지 도 를 강 조 하 는 6 approacht
대 화 참 여 를 통 해 대 화 를 시 작 , 진 행 , 종 결 하 는 방 법 을 학 습 시 켜 야 한 다 는 10160 approach7t 있 다 . 명 시 적 인
대 화 지 도 에 서는 알 맞 은 주 제 의 선 정 , 대 화 에 끼 어 들 기 , 화 제 바 꾸 기 , 대 화 종 결 하 기 등 을 다 룬 다 .

Conversation Analysis (CA) 다 화 분 석

Conversation analysis 15 concerned with describing the structure of conversational
interaction, including the sequential organization of talk and the ways that
speakers repair communication problems. CA includes turn-taking which means
avoiding either long silences or speaking at the same time when they talk, and
adjacency pair, the occurrence of two consecutive turns such as a question and
an answer. Other features identified by CA include conversational openings and

closing, and repair strategies.

대 화 분 석 이란 대 화 의 시 작 부 터 종 결 까 지 의 과 정 과 그 구 조 를 분 석 하 는 것 을 말 한 다 . 상 황과 문 화 에 맞 는 적 절 한
대 화 주제 선 택 하 기 , 상 대 방 의 “*EIOII 끼 어 들 기 , 화 제 바 꾸 기 , 대 화 종 결 하 기 의 전 략 뿐 아 니 라 상 대 방과 의 미 의
협 상 을 통 해 원 활 한 의 사 소 통 하 기 등 을 그 대 상 으 로 한 다 .

Co-operative principle 상 호 합 동 의 원 리

The co-operative principle is the principle that speakers try to co-operate with one
another. When people take part in conversations they do so on the assumption
that the other speakers will observe certain unstated “rules”. The co-operative
principle consists of four maxims which are quantity; make your contribution just as
informative as required, quality; make it that is true, relation; make it relevant, and

manner; avoid obscurity and ambiguity (be brief and orderly).

상호 협 동 의 원 리 는 두 사 람 이 상 의 대 화 에 서 성 공 적 인 대 화 를 하 기 위해 갖 추 어 야 할 대 화 상 의 격 률 을 말 한 다 .

Corpus

A corpus (plural corpora) is 3 collection of actually occurring texts, stores and
accessed by means of computers, and useful for investigation language use. The
use of corpora for researching language structure and use has led to development
of grammars and dictionaries that claim to be more reliable than their forbears,
in that they are based on attested data. One way that corpus information is
often presented is in the form of a concordance (a list of words, along with each

word’s immediate context).

Correction 수 정

Correction 15 3 form of feedback, when the teacher or another student provides
the correct version of an error. The amount and type of correction is closely
related to the teacher’s attitude 10 error. Where mistakes 316 seen as evidence of
bad habits, they need to be corrected overtly and fast. On the other hand, where
mistakes are viewed as a natural stage in the development of the learner’s inter-
language, and where learners are credited with having the capacity to work
things out for themselves, teachers may use a variety of strategies to elicit peer-
correction or self-correction. Second language acquisition research suggests that
lack of negative feedback may be a contributing factor to fossilization. Even if
corrections have little direct effect on acquisition, correction may serve to remind
learners to take accuracy seriously. And attention to accuracy (also called a focus

on form) is claimed to be a necessary condition for inter-language development.

Culture 문 화

Most definitions of culture distinguish between capital C-culture and small
c-culture. The former refers to those highly valued activities and artifacts related
to the arts. The latter refers to the beliefs, values, traditions, and practices shared
by a particular community. It is generally recognized that language are a mix
of universal concepts and of others that are more culturally specific. It is the
presence of the latter that explains why speakers of one language may perceive
the world and remember events differently from speakers of another language.
A strong version of the belief that language determines thought is known as
the Sapir-Whorf hypothesis. Nowadays, the claims of linguistic determinism 316

largely discredited. Otherwise, any kind of cross-cultural communication would
break down constantly. And learners seem relatively adept at making conceptual

adjustments when compelled to.

Dialogue ti st

In the language classroom, a dialogue is either the text of a two-way spoken
exchange, or it is the activity of having such an exchange. Dialogues have always
been a popular means for presenting and practicing language, one reason being
that dialogue is the most common and most widespread way that language is

used in real life.

담 화 는 두 사 람 이 상 의 담 화 자 간 에 서 일 어 난 것 을 말 하 며 교 실 내 연 습 활 동 의 많 은 부 분 이 대 화 형 식 으 로
진 행 된 다 . 대 화 는 가 장 일 반 적 인 의 사 소 통 의 방 식 이며 실 제 언 어 사 용 의 연 습 을 가 능 하 게 한 다 .

Direct method 직 점 교 수 범

This is an umbrella term 105 a wide 139086 of language teaching methods that
emerged in the later part of the nineteenth century. They shared the belief that
only the target language should be used in the classroom, and that therefore
translation should be avoided at all costs. Instead of translation, form-meaning
associations should 66 established using real objects, pictures, or demonstration.
The teacher’s 1016 was to maintain an extended “conversation” with the learners.
The direct method was a response to the growing demand for learning languages,
and offered a refreshing alternative to the bookish grammar-translation method
that prevailed at the time. In the USA, the direct method ingested behaviorist
theory and metamorphosed into audiolingualism. In the UL and Europe it became
the situational approach, but its core principle, the exclusive use of the target

language, survives as an article of faith amongst many teachers to this day.

## Page 297

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers

Discourse, Discourse analysis 담 화 분 석

Discourse 15 any connected piece of speaking or writing. Discourse analysis 15
principally the study of how such stretches of language achieve both cohesion
and coherence. Whereas traditional grammar is concerned only with sentences
and their components, discourse analysis seeks to identify patterns and
regularities of language “beyond the sentence”. It is closely related to, and partly
overlaps with, other textbased fields of study, including conversation analysis.
For the language teacher, the main implications of discourse analysis are in
the teaching of writing, especially with regard to the ways that texts are made

cohesive.

담 화 분 석 은 문 장 과 문장 사 이에 존 재 하 는 관 련 성과 응 집 력 을 분 석 한 다 . 같 은 문 장 이 더 라 도 서 로 다 른 문 맥

다 른 의 미 를 연 구 하 는 것 이 다 . 담 화 분 석 은 대 화 분 석 을 포 괄 하 여 사 용 되 기 도 한 다 .

Discourse marker =&l

Discourse markers (also called pragmatic markers) are words or expressions
like well, anyway, mean, actually, that normally come at the beginning of an
utterance, and function to orient the listener to what will follow. They do this
either by indicating some kind of change of direction in the talk, or by appealing
to the listener in some way. Linkers such as but, and, so, because, which connect
what has been said to what follows, are sometimes classified as discourse markers

as well.

것 을 예 측 할 수 있 다 . 적 절 한 담 화 표 시 자 의 사 용 은 상 대 방 의 담 화 를 이 해 하 는 데 도 움 이 될 뿐 만 아 니 라 지

늬 삐 Glossary

Display question

Display questions are questions asked by teachers in order that learners can
“display” their knowledge. They typically initiate classroom interaction, and is
called 30 IRF (interaction-response—follow up) sequence. In language classrooms,
display questions are usually aimed at finding out what learners can say in
the target language. Display questions contrast with real questions (also called
referential questions) which are motivated by the need to find out something
that the person asking the question doesn’t know. 50116 researchers suggest that
both the quality and quantity of communication in the classroom improves when

teachers ask more real questions than display questions.

Drill 반 복 연 습 활 동

A drill 165 repetitive oral practice of 3 language item, whether a sound, 3 word,
a phrase or a sentence structure. Drills that are targeted at enticed structures
are sometimes called pattern practice drills. Drills follow a prompt-response
sequence, where the prompt usually comes from the teacher, and the students
respond, either in chorus (a choral drill) or individually. A substitution drill
requires the students to substitute one element of the pattern with the prompt,
making any necessary adjustment. A variable substitution drill is the same,
but the prompts are not restricted to one element of the pattern. Drills were
defining feature of the audiolingual method, and were designed to reinforce
good language ‘habits’. With 6 demise 아 audiolingualism, drilling fell from
favor. However, many teachers—even those who subscribe to a communicative
approach—feel the need for some form of repetition practice of the kind that
drills provide. This may be for the purpose of developing accuracy, or as a form

of fluency training. Hence communicative drills were developed communicative

298  Build-up 영 어 교 육 론 Ｌ

## Page 299

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @ L—’

drill is still essentially repetitive, and focuses on 3 particular structure or pattern,

but it has an information gap element built.

Ellipsis 2

Ellipsis is the leaving out of elements of a sentence because they are either
unnecessary or because their sense can be worked out from the immediate
context. Ellipsis is very common in spoken language. Ellipsis of function words is

also a common feature of certain text types.

생 략 은 16% 에 서 불 필 요 하 거 나 예 측 가 능 한 표 현 을 생 략 하 는 것 을 말 한 다 . 주 로 구 어 에 서 많 이 사 용 된 다 .

"「

Error 오 류

An error is an instance of 016 learner’s language that dos not conform 10 accepted
norms of usage, and which is attributed to incomplete or faulty learning. Errors
are sometimes distinguished from mistakes, the former being due to lack
of knowledge, and the latter being due to the demands of performance. In
principle, the test of a mistake is whether the learner can self-correct effortlessly.
Errors can be categorized in a number of ways: an omission where an obligatory
element is left out, an addition where an element has been added unnecessarily,
a misselection error where the wrong item has been used, a misformation
where wrong form of the right word, and misordering error when sentence
components are in the wrong order. Errors are also classified according to their
possible cause. This is the particular concern of error analysis. Transfer errors are
those that result from the influence of the learner’s first language. On 6 other
hand, developmental errors are those that occur as a natural part of the learning
process. It used to be thought that all errors were transfer errors what were called

Appendix 01 Glossary 299

## Page 300

Appendix

interference. Research has shown, however, that there are certain errors that all
learners appear to make regardless of their first language, and in a predictable

chronological order. Many of these are due to the overgeneralization of a rule.

오 류는 학 생 들 의 발 화 에 서 부 정 확 한 표 현 이며 행 동 주 의 에 서는 오 류 를 잘 못 된 것 으 로 보 았 으 나 현 재 의 관 점 에 서는
류 도 학 습 자 의 중 간 언어 발 달 의 한 과 정 으 로 긍 정 적 으 로 보 고 있 다 . 교 사 의 오 류 수 정 의 정 도 는 어 느 오 류 에
해 , 어 느 정 도 로 수 정 을 하 느 냐 가 주 요 문 제 인 데 오 류 수 정 의 정 도 는 수 업 목 표 에 따 라 달 라 져 야 한 다 . 정 확 성에

Experiential learning z# 중 심 교 수 법

Experiential learning is 3 general term for “deep-end” approaches to learning that
rate direct practical experience over the learning and application of abstract rules.
10 language learning terms, this might take the form of task-based learning, of
discovery-learning, or of content-based learning. Experiential language learning
shares with mentalist theories of learning a belief in the value of learners actively
working things out for themselves. It also shares with humanism a commitment to
whole-person learning, and, with critical pedagogy, a belief in the transformative
power of direct experience rather than simply applying knowledge that has been

“handed down” by some higher authority.

경 험 중 심 교 수 법 은 교 사 의 명 시 적 인 지 식 의 전 달이 아 닌 학 습 자 스 스 로 가 경 험 을 통 해 새 로 운 내 용 을 학 습 하 는
것 을 말 한 다 . 예 를 들 어 문 법 지 도에 있 어 서 교 사 가 규 칙 을 알 려 주 는 것 이 아 니 라 학 습 자 가 다 량 의 예 문 을
접 하 거 나 직접 의 사 소 통 을 해 보 면 서 규 칙 을 발 견 해 나 가 는 것 이 다 . 640606043 leaming2 언 어 를 총 체 적 으 로

Facilitation 학 습 의 촉 진

To facilitate 3 process, such 35 language learning, is to help make it happen.
Facilitation is a way of thinking about teaching that recognizes the fact that
teachers do not directly cause learning, but that they can provide the conditions
in which learning happens. The teacher facilitates the process by managing the

learning, where the teacher’s 1016 15 primarily that of a consultant, providing

learner with the language they need 10 construct their own conversations.

Feedback 피 드 백 ( 교 정 적 정 보 )

Feedback is the information, either immediate or delayed, that learners get on
their performance. At least some of this feedback may have a long-term effect
on their knowledge of the language. Traditionally, feedback takes the form of
correction. Correction is called negative feedback: it is 3 clear message that the
learner has produced an error. But feedback can also be positive. Feedback can
be explicit or it can be implicit since the teacher does not overtly indicate that
the learner has made an error. Researchers into second language acquisition are
in two minds, however. If the learners’ errors elicit only positive feedback, and
therefore go unnoticed and uncorrected, these errors may become fossilized.
Other researchers, however, have argued that even explicit negative feedback
has no long-term effect either. This is because the learner’s developing mental
grammar is not yet “ready” for 6 correction. To counter this argument,
supporters of negative feedback argue that, while the effect of correction might
not be either immediate or predictable, constant “nagging” serves to remind
learners to pay attention to form. And paying attention to form is good for them

in the long run.

내 의 피 드 백 은 학 습 자 의 발 화 와 언어 수 행 에 대 해 교 사 가 관 련된 정 보 를 제 공 하 는 것 으 로 긍 정 적 인 피 드 백 ,
인 피 드 백 , 부 정 적 인 피 드 백 으 로 LEHCH 또 한 정 의 적 인 피 드 백 과 인 지 적 인 피 드 백 이 있 는 데 학 습 자 의

Fluency =28

If someone is said to be fluent in a language, or to speak a language fluently,
it is generally understood that they are able to speak the language idiomatically
and accurately, without undue pausing, without an intrusive accent, and in a
manner appropriate to the context. Fluency is primarily the ability to produce
and maintain speech in real time. Classroom activities that target fluency need to
prepare the learner for real-time speech production. Learning and memorizing
lexical chunks, including useful conversational gambits, is one approach.
Drills may help here, as will some types of communicative activity that involve
repetition. Some interactive and competitive language games have this effect.
Drama activities, such as role-plays, recreate conditions of real-time language
use, and are therefore good for developing fluency. Finally, learners can achieve

greater fluency from learning a repertoire of communication strategies.

유 창 성 있 는 말 하 기 는 주 로 자 신 이 하 고 자 하 는 말 을 막 힘 과 끊 김 이 없 이 유 창 하 게 표 현 을 할 수 있 는 밀 하 기
능 력 을 일 컨 는 다 . 유 창 성 있 는 말 하 기 능 력 에 는 개 별 철 자 의 명 확 한 발 음 도 중 요 하 지만 담 화 맥 락 에 서 의 적 절 한
강 세 , 억 양 등 의 초 분 절 적 인 요 소도 크 게 영 향 을 끼 친 다 .

Formulaic Ianguage

Formulaic language refers to those sequences of two or more words that operate
as a single unit. This means they are stored 10 the memory, and retrieved, 35 if
they were one-word vocabulary items. Also called (lexical) chunks, multi-word
units, readymades, prefabricated language and holophrases, formulaic language
can be classified into collocations, phrasal verbs, idioms, and discourse markers.

Fossilization 화 서 화

A fossilized error is 006 that has become 3 permanent feature of a learner’s
interlanguage. There are various theories as to what causes fossilization. It has
been hypothesized that the lack of instruction, specially the lack of a focus on
form, is the main cause. This is used as an argument for giving explicit attention
to grammar. Another theory is that fossilization may be due to the lack of
negative feedback on errors, a view that is used to justify correction. Fossilization
may also be due to the fact that learners have not been “pushed” to make their

output more accurate.

화 석 화 현 상 은 학 습 자 의 오 류 가 수 정 되 지 못 하 고 학 습 자 의 인 지 구 조 속 에 영 구 히 자 리 잡는 것 을 말 한 다 .
화 석 화 의 원 인 은 명 시 적 인 문 법 지 도 , 오 류 에 대 한 부 정 적 인 피 드 백 , 상 호 작 용 속 의 pushed output®] 부 재 등이
있 다
찌 나 .

Function 기 능

The function of 3 language item 185 its communicative purpose. Language is more
than simply forms and their associated meanings. It is also the communicative
uses to which there forms and meanings are put. There is no one-to-one match
between form and function. Assigning a function to a text or an utterance usually

requires knowledge of the context in which the text is used.

언 어 의 기 능 은 의 사 소 통에 있 다 . 의 사 소 통 은 상호 간 의 의 미 전 달 에 의 해 이 루 어 지는 것 인 데 성 공 적 인 의 사 소 통 을
위 해 서는 담 화 내 에 서 의 의 미 파 악 이 중 요 하 다 .

Functional syllabus 7is 34 교 수 요 목

A functional syllabus 15 3 syllabus based around a list of language functions such
as asking for information; making request; greeting people. Functional syllabuses
were first developed to support a communicative approach. In contrast to the
prevailing structural syllabuses of the time, they were meaning based rather than

Appendix 01 Glossary 303

## Page 304

form based. They were often combined with language notions to form what was

called a functional-notional syllabus.

Function word 기 능 어

Function words, 3150 called grammar words, 316 those words which have a
mainly grammatical function. They contrast with content words, which carry
the main informational load. Function words 316 auxiliary verb, determiners,

pronouns, preposition, conjunctions, and adverbs.

기 능 어 는 내 용 어 와 는 반 대 로 단 어 가 지 니 는 의 미 가 없 거 나 문 장 에 서 중 요 한 의 미 를 지 니 지 못 하 는 단 어 들 로 주 로

사 용 된 다 .

Grammar-translation method 문 범 번 역 식 교 수 범

Grammar translation 15 3 language teaching method that developed out of the
way that classical languages such as Latin and Greek were traditionally taught.
The grammar part comes from the fact that grammar is taught deductively and
that grammatical accuracy is highly prioritized. Grammar-translation was seriously
challenged by the advent of the direct method. Thus, inductive presentations
would replace deductive ones, whole texts would replace isolated sentences, and
there would be a focus not only on reading and writing but also on speaking and

listening.

고 전 어 를 가 르 치 던 교 수 법 에 서 유 래 한 문 법 번 역 식 교 수 법 은 학 습 의 주 요 내 용 을 문 법 지 도와 모 국 어 로 의 번 역 을
대 상 으 로 한 다 . 언 어 형 태 가 연 역 적 인 방 법 으 로 먼 저 제 시 되 고 정 확 성 을 수 업 의 목 표 로 하 는 데 이에 대 한 반 발 로
직 접 교 수 법 이 등 장 하 였 다 .

Groupwork 1= 활 동

Groupwork is a form of classroom interaction where learners work together,
part of all of the time, in small groups. The best size for a group is probably
from three to five learners: anything larger may mean that not all learners will
contribute often or equally. Groupwork works best if there is a clear outcome to
the task, such as making a decision, performing to the rest of the class. It can be
a good idea to assign roles to individual members, and also important that the
seating arrangement permits all the members of the group to see and hear one
another. Finally, the teacher needs to monitor groupwork to ensure that learners
are on-task, to be available to answer questions, and to provide feedback

(including correction) on task performance.

그 룹 활 동 은 학 생 들 간 의 상 호 작 용 을 도 모 하 는 가 장 흔 한 교 실 활 동 중 의 하 나 이 다 . 하 나 의 그 룹 에 는 4~6 명 ,
특 히 5 명 이 적 당 한 데 그 이 유 는 학 생 들 에 게 적 절 한 발 언 의 기 회 가 부 여 되 며 특 정 학 생 에 게 역 할 이 집 중 되 지 않 는
적 절 한 수 이 기 때 문 이 다 . 보 다 효 과 적 인 그 룹 활 동 을 위 해 서는 학 생 들 에 게 과 업 에 대 한 명 시 적 인 안 내 를 해 주 고

그 룹 의 leaderE 정 해 줌 으 로 써 그 룹 활 동 을 보 다 MUY 있 게 할 수 있 다 .

Immersion & 프 로 그 램

An immersion program 15 one in which children are taught some or all of their
school subjects in a language that is not their mother tongue. It is aimed at
fostering bilingualism. Immersion should be distinguished from submersion,
which is what happens when individuals who speak one language are placed
in a situation in which their education is mediated using another. In general,
immersion education is not prejudicial, either to the ongoing development of the
pupils’ first Janguage, or 10 their overall academic performance. Moreover, they
achieve a near-native level of understanding of the second language, although, in

production, their grammatical accuracy falls short of native speakers.

교 과 내 용 을 영 어로 가 르 치 는 몰 입 프 로 그 램 은 이 중 병 행 사 용 을 목 적 으 로 한 다 . Immersion program0| 비 영 어 권

것 을 말 한 다 . 따 라 서 후 자 는 학 습 자 들 의 모 국 어 와 모 국 문 화 는 배 제 된 채 목 표 어 가 대 신 하 는 반 면 , 전 자 는 모 국 어 와

Individual learner differences 학 습 자 개 인 차

Individual learners 316 different, with very different learning styles, abilities,
needs and drives. The key factors are often grouped into biological factors
such as age and gender; personality factors such as confidence and self-esteem;
cognitive factors such as aptitude, learning style and memory; and affective
factors such as motivation and anxiety. One of the outcomes of this research
has been the development of learner training procedures, which target those
factors that are susceptible to change and improvement. These include the
learner’s use of learning strategies, or techniques of improving memory. Another
way of responding to the fact that learners are all different has been in the
individualization of learning, through, for example, one-to-one teaching, and the

use of self-access centers.

학 습 자 개 개 인 은 학 습 스 타 일 , 53, 요 구 뿐 만 아 니 라 자 신 감 과 동 기 등 의 정 의 적 측 면에 있 어 서 도 저 마 다 차 이 를
가 지 고 있 다 . 학 습 자 들 의 이 러 한 차 이 점 을 고 려 하 기 위 해 서는 되 도록 다 양 한 종 류 의 과 업 과 수 준 별 과 제 를 제 공 할
필 요 가 있 다 .

Information exchanging 정 보 의 교 환

Exchanging information is 006 of the key functions of language. Language that is
used in this way is called transactional language. It is typically performed by the
asking of questions and by answering with statements. Teaching learners how to
ask for and give information is a core component of most syllabuses, tight from
the outset. Popular activities for practicing this function include dialogues and

information gap activities.

언 어 의 대 표 적 인 기 능 인 정 보 의 교 환 은 대 인 관 계 의 유 지 를 목 적 으 로 하 는 interpersonal languageot= 달 리 특 정
정 보 의 전 달 을 포 함 하 고 있 다 . 정 보 교 환 의 연 습 활 동 은 대 화 나 정 보 격 차 활 동 을 통 해 이 루 어 진 다 .

Input 2=

Input is the spoken or written language that learners are exposed to. You can
not learn a language without input. In his input hypothesis, the linguist Stephen
Krashen argues that input is all that is necessary for language acquisition to take

306 Buildup 영 어 교 육 론 1

## Page 307

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @ L‘

place. But the input must be comprehensible, and it must contain grammatical
forms that are one step more advanced than the current state of the learners’
interlanguage. The modifications such as simplified, delivered at a slower pace
and more elaborated input may assist interlanguage development. Michael Long,
argues that input is most effective when it has been made comprehensible

through negotiation of meaning.

인 지 주 의 이 론 에 따 르 면 , inputg intakedt?| 위 해 서는 의 식 적 인 noticing0] 필 수 적 이 다 . Intakes inpute|

Interaction 상 호 작 용

Interaction occurs when learners communicate with one another. According
to the communicative approach, learner-learner interaction through small-
group interaction, where learners solve tasks using language, was all that was
needed to promote language acquisition. Long’s interaction hypothesis claims
that tasks that promote negotiation of meaning are beneficial by providing
comprehensible input. Long subscribes Krashen’s view that comprehensible input
is necessary for language acquisition. But, unlike Krashen, Long argues for the
need for interaction, primarily because it is a site for negotiation meaning. The
interactional modifications that are involved in negotiating meaning are known
as discourse repair strategies. Teacher-learner interaction consists of sequences of
display questions. According to socio-cultural learning theory, learners should be
given more control over the direction of the discourse and the choice of topic,
30 that the teacher’s role should be more facilitative. This includes providing 06

interactional support or scaffolding.

어 습 득 은 타 인 과 의 상 호 작 용 - 발 화 와 피 드 백 을 통 한 의 미 의 협 상 , 타 인 의 =8 등 을 통 해 가 능 하 다 . 교 사 는

Interlanguage 중 간 인어

Interlanguage is the term 4568 10 describe the grammatical system 4131 a
learner creates 10 the course 아 learning 3 target language. It is neither their first
language system, nor the target language system, but occupies 3 transitional
point between the two. This interlanguage is seen as an independent system in
its own right, and not simply a degenerate form of the target language. It reflects
the learner’s evolving system of rules. Some 아 these rules may 66 influenced
by the first language through transfer, others by the target language. One way
that interlanguages show that they are systematic is that they follow predictable
stages. Also, interlanguages 316 constantly evolving (dynamic). When they stop
doing so, they stabilize, or even fossilize, at a point some way from the target.

중 간 언 어 는 목 표 어 에 대 해 갖 고 있 는 불 완 전 한 지 식 체 계 , 즉 모 국 어 의 언어 체 계 와 는 다 르 면 서 목 표 어 의
언어 체 계 라 하 기 에 는 불 완 전 하 기 때 문에 모 국 어 와 목 표 어 의 사 이에 위 치 한 중 간 언 어 라 부 른 다 . 중 간 언 어 는
변 이 성 ( 오 류 의 자 유 로 운 출 현 ), 체 계 성 ( 오 류 라 하 더 라 도 나 름 의 규 칙 을 토 대 로 형 성 ), 역 동 성 ( 규 칙 들 이 끊 임 없 이

Language acquisition 인 이 습 득

According to Stephen Krashen’s distinction, acquisition means the non-conscious
and “natural” process of internalizing the rules of a language, as in first language
acquisition. On the other hand, learning involves conscious, usually classroom,
study, including attending to rules of grammar. Krashen argues that first language
acquisition and second language can only be acquired. According to Krashen,
learning plays no part in the process. The only value of learning rules is that you
can use these to check or monitor your output. The claim that acquisition and
learning are separate, independent processes, that do not influence one another,

is called the no-interface position.

생 득 주 의 에 따 르 면 언어 습 득 이란 언어 규 칙 들 의 자 연 스 러 운 내 재 화 현 상 이 다 . 마 치 모 국 어 가 시 간 이 흐 름 에
따 라 자 연 스 럽 게 습 득 이 되- 1 처 럼 목 표 어 도 많 은 언 어 에 의 많 은 노 출 을 통 해 습 득 이 가 능 하 다 고 보이기

때 문에 인 위 적 인 문 법 지 도 는 불 필 요 한 것 이라 보 았 다 . 하 지만 인 지 주 의 자 들 은 언 어 에 의 노 출 만 으 로는 언 어 습 득 이
불 가 능 하 며 언어 요 소 에 주 의 집 중 하 여 내 재 화 하 는 000009 과 문 법 지 도와 연 습 을 통 해 서 습 득 이 가 능 하 다 고 보았다_

Learner-centered instruction, Learner-centeredness 학 습 자 중 심 교 수

Learner-centered instruction aims to give learners 101016 say 10 31635 that 316
traditionally considered the domain of the teacher by providing learners with
greater autonomy. For example, 3 learner-centered curriculum would involve
learners in negotiating decisions relation to the choice of syllabus content, of
materials, of activity-types, and of assessment procedures. Learner-centeredness
also describes ways of organizing classroom interaction so that the focus is
directed away from the teacher, and on to the learners, who perform tasks in

pairs or small groups.

학 습 자 중 심 의 교 수 는 교 사 중 심 의 전 통 적 교 수 법 에 서 탈 피 하 여 학 습 자 가 자 신 의 학 습 의 주 도 권 을 갖 고 있 는

Learner training #&xt 22

The aim of learner training is to help learners make the most of the learning
opportunities that are available to them. In the long term, it is directed at
achieving autonomy in language learning. Typical learner training procedures
include: having learners complete questionnaires to help them identify their
own learning style; showing learners how to get the most out of resources;
training them in effective reading and listening strategies; and experimenting with

techniques to aid memorization.

교 사 는 학 습 자 훈 련 을 통 해 학

전 략 지 도 하 기 등 다 양 한 방 법 이 있 다 .

Learning strategy ==

Learning strategies are techniques that learners consciously apply in order to
enhance their learning. They are often grouped according to whether they are
cognitive, meta-cognitive or social (affective) strategies. Cognitive strategies
are those that are linked to the way when learners process data and perform

specific tasks in the target language. Meta-cognitive strategies are those that are

Appendix 01 Glossary 309

## Page 310

Appendix

늬 삐 Glossary

used to regulate and manage learning in general. Reflecting on the learning
process is also a metacognitive strategy: this may take the form of keeping a
language-learning journal. Social strategies are those that learners use in order
to interact with other learners or native speakers, such as asking for repetition
or clarification. Affective strategies are those that they use to give themselves

encouragement and to deal with anxiety.

학 습 자 들 이 효 과 적 인 학 습 을 위해 사 용 하 는 학 습 자 전 략 은 인 지 적 전 략 , 상 위 인 지 전 략 , 사 회 정 의 적 전 략 으 로
나 된 다 . 인 지 적 전 략 은 과제 수 행 에 직 접 적 으 로 관 련된 전 략 들 을 , 사 회 정 의 적 전 략 은 타 인 과 의 상 호 작 용 이 나
자 신 의 학 습 에 의 격 려 등 을 말 한 다 . 상 위 인 지 전 략 은 이 모 두 를 아 우 르 는 개 념 으 로 학 습 전 반 에 걸 쳐 학 습 을

계 획 하 고 점 검 하 고 학 습 과 정 을 평 가 하 는 전 략 을 가 리 킨 다 .

Learning style 학 습 양 식

Your learning style is your preferred way of learning. 17065 of learning style
are often presented in the form of polarities such as analytic versus global
thinkers, rule-users versus data gatherers, reflective versus impulsive learners,
extrovert versus introverted learner, and verbal versus visual learners. Attempts
have been made to group these polarities and relate them to brain lateralization.
So, a bias towards leftbrain processing correlates with analytic, rule-forming
and verbal learners, while a bias towards right-brain processing correlates with
their opposite. So far, though, there is no convincing evidence that any of these
dispositions correlates with specific learning behaviors. Nor has it been shown
that a preference in one area predicts success in language learning. The best that
can 66 said is that, if the learner’s preferred learning style 15 out of synch with the
type of instruction on offer, then success is much less likely than if the two are
well matched. This supports the case for an eclectic approach, on the one hand,

and the individualization of learning, on the other.

학 습 자 의 학 습 양 식 은 분 석 적 학 습 / 총 체 적 학 습 , 규 칙 위 주 학 습 / 자 료 기반 학 습 , 숙 고 형 / 충 동 적 , 외 향 적 / 내 향 적 ,

언어 중 심 학 습 / 이 미 지 B4 학 습 으 로 LIHCE 이 들 양 식 은 주 로 좌 뇌 와 우 뇌 가 학 습 에 얼 마 나 더 큰 영 향 을

Lexical approach 이 휘 기반 접 근 법

A lexical approach to language teaching 15 one that has chosen vocabulary
35 the main focus for syllabus design and classroom teaching. This contrasts
with traditional approaches, which usually focus on grammar. This lexical 6135
emerged out of developments in corpus linguistics, especially research into
collocation and word frequency.

Memorization 기 억 , 암 기

the memorization of meaningful words, phrases, and even sentences is now

considered to be an essential ingredient of language learning.

특 정 정 보 , 지 식 을 기 억 하 는 과 정 으 로 전 통 적 인 관 점 에 서는 문 법 규 칙 등 의 단 순 암 기를 통 한 언 어 학 습 을

Mentalism, mentalist theory 실 리 주 의 , 이 성 주 의

Mentalism is the theory that language is an innate property of mind. It is primarily
associated with the work of Noam Chomsky, and represents a reaction to a

purely behaviorist view of language acquisition.

Mentalism 학 습 자 의 관 찰 가 능 한 발 화 에 만 초 점 을 두 는 행 동 주 의 에 반 기를 들며 등 장 하 여 인 간 의 보 이 지 않 는

Metalanguage 게 타 언어

Metalanguage is the language that is used to talk about language, and 15 better
known as terminology, especially grammar terms such as adjective, auxiliary, etc.
In the past, methods such as the direct method and audiolingualism rejected any

role for explicit knowledge, and, by association, metalanguage.

Method 교 수벌

A method is 35 system for the teaching 이 3 language that is based either on
particular theory of language or on a particular theory of learning, or on both.

312 Buildup 영 어 교 육 론 Ｌ

## Page 313

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @

These theories will underpin choices of syllabus type, materials, and classroom
activities. Method should not be confused with a course book: a course book is
simply the material support for a method. Nor should method be confused with
methodology, which is a general word to describe classroom practices such as
classroom management, irrespective of the particular method that a teacher is
using. Approach denotes a more general theoretical orientation, while a method

is just one way that the approach is realized in practice.

Mixed ability 이 질 적 집 단 교 실

ability classes. Mixed ability classes should 66 distinguished 601 classes of mixed
levels, where students with different levels of proficiency are grouped together.
Mixed ability classes become 3 problem when the diversity threatens the general

dynamics of the classroom.

## Page 314

Appendix

—J 삐 Glossary

Motivation 동 기

Motivation is what drives learners to achieve 3 goal, and is 3 key factor
determining success or failure in language learning. With regard to long-term
goals, a distinction is often made between instrumental motivation and integrative
motivation. Instrumental motivation is when the learner has a functional
objective, such as passing an exam or getting a job. Integrative motivation, on the
other hand, is when the learner wants to be identified with the target language
community. Intersecting with these two motivational orientations are two different
sources of motivation: intrinsic (e.g., the pleasure of doing a task for its own

sake) and extrinsic.

학 습 에 있 어 서 동 기 란 학 습 을 하 게 끔 하 는 원 동 력 을 말 하 며 언 어 학 습 의 성 공 여 부 를 질 하 는 가 장 중 요 한 요 소

Multiple intelligences 다 종 지 능

The theory of multiple intelligences (MI) views intelligence 35 being multi-
dimensional. Proponents of this view have identified at least seven different kinds
of intelligence that individuals possess in different strengths and combinations.
These are verbal/linguistic, logical/mathematical, visual/spatial, bodily/kinesthetic,

musical/rhythmic, interpersonal, and intrapersonal intelligence.

Natural approach == 접 근 범

The term “natural approach” attempted 10 mirror the processes of learning a first
language. Translation and grammar explanations were rejected, learners were
exposed to sequences of actions, and the spoken form was taught before the

## Page 315

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @ L—

written form. Learners were initially exposed to meaningful language, not forced
to speak until they felt ready to, and not corrected or given explicit grammar
instruction. There included the importance of comprehensible input, and of

promoting positive affect in the learning process.

Needs analysis 요 구 분 석

Needs analysis 18 the process of specifying the learners’ language needs in
advance of designing a course for them. The analysis can then be used to
materials, and also the methodology. Finally, the needs analysis can be used in

the design of assessment and evaluation procedures.

Notional syllabus 구 녕 중 심 교 수 요 목

A notional syllabus 18 3 syllabus that is organized according to general 31635
of meaning that are used in most grammars. Notions are universal concepts
such as location, frequency, possibility and duration. These notional categories
were combined with language functions—such as requesting, suggesting, and
apologizing—to form what became known as functional-notional syllabuses.

These syllabuses formed the backbone of the communicative approach.

One-to-one-teaching 112+

One-to-one teaching is individualized instruction, in contrast to the teaching of
small or large groups. There are obvious advantages for the student: students
have the undivided attention of the teacher, they have optimal opportunities for
participation, and the classes can be tailored to their particular needs, pace and
learning style. Teachers do not have to deal with the kinds of diversity frequently
encountered in groups, such as mixed level and mixed ability.

Output hypothesis

Output is the language that learners produce, either spoken or written. The
output hypothesis is the theory that output, especially spoken output, is
necessary condition for language acquisition. Merrill Swain argues that learners
also need to be pushed to produce comprehensible output as well. If learners are
simply exposed to comprehensible input, they may understand the message but
overlook the way the message is formulated. Being pushed to produce language

puts learners in a better position to notice the gaps in their language knowledge.

Paralinguistics

Paralinguistics is the study of non-linguistic means of vocal communication.
This includes the use of different kinds of voice quality, loudness, intonation,
and tempo to convey particular emotions and attitudes. The term is also used to
describe non-vocal features of communication, such 35 gesture, facial expression,

and eye contact.

Personalization

When you personalize language you 456 it to talk about your knowledge,
experience and feelings. Personalization creates better classroom dynamics. This

fence more motivation rather than the characters in course books.

PPP model

PPP stands for presentation-practice-production. In the PPP model, a pre-selected
grammar item is first presented to the learners through demonstration. Its rules
of form and use are either explained or elicited for the learners. The item is then
practiced 10 isolation, and with 30 emphasis on accuracy. Teacher control 15
gradually relinquished, and activities are set up to encourage free production of

the grammar item in context, and with an emphasis on fluency.

가 르 칠 언어 요 소 들 이 먼 저 제 시 된 후 이 를 바 탕 으 로 연 습 활 동 과 확 장 된 00 냐 을 생 성 하 는 단 계 로 이 루 어 진 2

Practice zs2s

If you practice a skill, you experience doing it a number of times in order
to gain control of it. There are different kinds of practice, such as controlled
practice vs free practice and mechanical vs meaningful/communicative practice.
In controlled practice, language that is being practiced is restricted to what
has just been presented. Practice is controlled because learners’ participation
is overtly managed and monitored by the teacher. Free practice, on the other
hand, allows learners a measure of creativity, and the opportunity to integrate

the new item into their existing language system. Mechanical practice is a form

318 Build-up 영 어 교 육 론 Ｌ

## Page 319

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @

of controlled practice, where the focus is less on the meaning of an item than on
manipulating it component parts. Meaningful practice requires learners to display
some understanding of what the item that they are practicing actually means.
Communicative practice involves the learners interacting in order to complete

some kind of task, such as in an information gap activity.

연 습 활 동 은 55| XS54 (automalticity)S 위 한 필 요 조 건 으 로 충 분 한 연 습 은 언 어 습 득 에 도 움 이 된 다 는 것 에 는
이 견 이 없 으 나 교 사 는 목 적 에 맞 게 적 절 한 연 습 활 동 을 사 용 해 야 한 다 . 연 습 활 동 은 학 습 활 동 에 대 한 교 사 의 통제
정 도에 w2t controlled, free practice®, 내 용 의 유 의 미 성에 따 라 mechanical, meaningful, communicative
practice2 LFHC,

Pragmatics 82

Pragmatics is the study of how language is used and interpreted by its users in
real world situations. It attempts to explain how exchanges in a conversation
might make sense to the people who are engaged in them. The fact that semantic
meaning literal meaning of an utterance) and pragmatic meaning (intended

meaning) may not correspond is central to the study of pragmatics.

언 어 는 같 은 표 현 이 라 고 하 더 라 도 상 황 에 따 라 의 미 하 는 바 가 달 라 지 는 데 화 용 론 은 이 러 한 의 미 의 차 이 를 주
그 연 구 대 상 으 로 한 다 . 예 를 들 면 ‘Thank you for not smoking’ol2ts 문 장 은 외 현 적 으 로는 담 배 를 피 우 지

금 지 ( 아 아 10000)) 의 기 능 을 하 고 있 다 .

Presentation # 4

The presentation stage of a lesson is the stage when a new language item—
typically a grammar structure—is introduced 10 the learners. Presentation is the
first stage in the PPP model of lesson design. Grammar presentations can be
either deductive or inductive. The former begins with a statement of the rule and
is followed by examples. The latter begins with examples from which learners
work out the rule. In a deductive presentation the rule is always made explicit,

but in an inductive presentation the rule may be left unstated.

Reference 지 시

Reference 15 the relation between language 101015 and things in the 1231 world.
Some language is highly referential, in the sense that we can identify the
particular person or thing that is referred to, as in That towel belongs to me. But
words do not refer to specific things, rather a generic one. Thus, in I need a new
towel the referent of the word towel is not a specific towel but a generic towel.
Learning a second language is largely the matching of new forms to existing
concepts. But, of course, the process can be facilitated by using real things

(realia) or pictures of them (aids) to represent the concepts.

10/6!' 이 라 는 문 장 에 서 3 new towel2 실 재 하 는 towel0| 아 닌 추 상 적 인 대 상 을 가 리 킨 다 . 언 어 학 습 에 는 이 러 한
추 상 적 인 지 시 대 상도 포 함 되 어 있 기 때 문에 실 물 교 재 나 사 진 등 을 이 용 하 면 추 상 적 인 개 념 의 습 득 에 도 움 이 된 다 .

Reflection, Reflective teaching = Az, 반 성 적 교 수

When you reflect on your teaching, you think back on it, in order to understand
it better, and to take steps to improve it. Is is claimed that self-directed reflection
is a characteristic of professional expertise. One way of encouraging reflection is

through the keeping of a teaching journal.

Repair 발 화 의 수 정

If you repair an utterance, you correct or modify what you have just said, so
as 10 make it more accurate or more intelligible. Repair can be self-initiated or
otherinitiated, 10 non-classroom contexts repair may be triggered by communication
breakdowns with other speakers such as comprehension check, confirmation check,
and clarification request. According to the interaction hypothesis, this sort of repair

work provides “raw material” for language acquisition.

발 화 의 수 정 은 자 신 의 발 화 를 더 명 확 하 고 정 확 하 게 하 기 위해 사 용 되 는 의 사 소 통 전 략 으 로 대 화 담 화 자 의
반 응 이 나 요 구 에 의 해 서 일 어 나 지만 발 화 자 스 스 로 가 오 류 를 발 견 하 고 수 정 할 수 도 QICH Long2 상 호 작 용 가 설 을
통 해 이 러 한 ' 수 정 ' 을 통 한 의 사 소 통 활 동 은 언 어 습 득 의 가 장 중 요 한 요 소라 보 았 다 .

Repetition 받 복
Repetition underlies many language learning activities, and audiolingualism
developed drills, which the common characteristic of was repetition. In fact,
researchers into memory have found that rote repetition is a relatively inefficient
way of learning. Unless the learner makes some deliberate attempt to organize
the material being learned, no amount of repetition will guarantee that it is
moved into long-term memory.

굶 무 10

865 ucturing 재 구 조 화

If a system restructures, it responds 10 new information by re-organizing itself
50 35 to accommodate the new information. Restructuring is the term used 10
cognitive learning theory to describe what seems to happen 10 the learner’s
developing interlanguage system, as it adapts to new input. But it may result in
what is called backsliding, which is what happens when the learner over-applies

the rule (or overgeneralizes it).

Revision, Review =&

Revision is the process previously studied material, especially in advance of a
test. In fact, one of the arguments in favor of testing is that it encourages revision,
since the regular recycling of material makes it easier to recall. However, if the
revision consists of little more than rote memorization of facts it 15 unlikely to

serve much long-term usefulness, either for learning or for testing purposes.

장 기 기 억 에 는 도 움 이 되 지 못 한 다 . 복 습 은 학 습 한 직 후 에 일 어 날 수 록 , 장 기 적 으 로 일 어 날 수 록 성 공 적 인 학 습 에
도 움 이 된 다 .

Schema 인 지 도 식

A schema (plural schemata) 18 the way that knowledge about a topic or concept
is represented and organized in the mind. Schemata help us make sense of
experience, and hence they are crucial in comprehension. A schema constitutes
part of what is called the top-down knowledge of a text. If students do not have

322 Build-up 영 어 교 육 론 Ｌ

the schema, or 표 the schema is represented differently 10 their own culture, or if
they simply fail to access it, they will have to rely on bottom-up processing alone,
ie, working out the meaning from the vocabulary and grammar. Thus, teachers

can help learners understand a text by contextual information.

Second language 제 2 인 어

560010 language refers to any language that has been learned subsequent to the
acquisition of the first language. It also contrasts with foreign language, especially
in the terms ESL and EFL, where the former refers to the learning of English
by learners who are living in an English-speaking environment and who need

English in order to become integrated into that environment.

Second Language Acquisition (SLA) xizeioi a=

SLA is the study of how second languages are acquired. It is a relatively new field
of study, emerging in the wake of the failure of behaviorism to offer a satisfactory
explanation of either first or second language acquisition. Since the demise of
behaviorism, a great many new theories have emerged to account for SLA. They
fall into three broad groups: universal grammar (UG), cognitive learning theory

and socio-cultural learning theory.

큰 흐 름 으 로 구 분 이 된 다 . 행 동 주 의 는 제 2 언 어 습 득 을 습 관 의 형 성 으 로 , 인 지 주 의 는 문 법 규 칙 의 내 재 화 에 따 른

Self-access 061761 자 기 중 심 학 습

A self-access center is that part of 3 language teaching institution that is allocated
to self-directed study. It is usually equipped with books, computers, video
monitors, and audio equipment. Self-access centers were popular at the height
of the learner autonomy movement, but they are expensive to run and maintain,
and many have become re-absorbed into the institution’s library or turned into

internet rooms.

자 기 학 습 은 교 재 , 컴 퓨 터 , 비 디 오 등 다 양 한 교 수 자 료 의 개 발 로 발 달 되 었 다 . 자 기 학 습 은 학 습 자 의 자 기 학 습 에 대 한

Silent period 침 묵 시기

The 581601 period refers to the fact that children learning their first language 80
through a lengthy period simply listening before they venture their first words.
The same phenomenon has been observed in L2 learners. Some researchers
have argued that this silent period is a necessary stage in language acquisition. It
provides an opportunity to comprehend input, a prerequisite for the development

이 the learner’s internal grammar.

Silent way 침 묵 교 수 법

The Silent Way 185 normally grouped among 416 humanistic approaches 10
language learning. According to this way, language learning is a personal, even
mystical process, one that is self-initiated and self-directed: “Only the learner can
do the learning.” Hence, the teacher’s role is that of 3 technician or facilitator. It
is the teacher’s deliberately unobtrusive presence and minimal interventions that

give the method its name.

Skills 언 어 기 능

A language skill 18 3 way 10 which language is used. Language skills contrast with
language systems. The systems include the grammar, vocabulary, and phonology,
whereas the skills are customarily divided into the two productive skills: speaking

and writing, and the two receptive skills: listening and reading.

Socio-cultural learning theory 사 회 문 화 적 학 습 이론

Socio-cultural theory 168310 learning 35 being 3 500131 process through 500131
interaction in which the learner is assisted from dependency towards autonomy.
Unlike mentalism, socio-cultural theory situates the learning process firmly in
its social context. According to this view, all learning is mediated through social
and cultural activity. Through this shared activity, new knowledge is jointly
constructed, until the learner is in a position to appropriate it, at which stage the

scaffolding can gradually be dismantled.

비 고 츠 키 는 사 회 문 화 적 학 습 이 론 을 통 해 학 습 자 는 보 다 뛰 어 어《뽄항\』가† 부 모 , 보 다 뛰 어 난 동 료 ) 와 의

상 호 작 용 과 정 속 에 서 주 어 지는 도 움 (60081009106) 을 통 해 했쏘만의 지 식 을 구 축 하 고 27[)( 근 접 발 달 영 역 ) 을 넘 어 서
학 습 을 하 게 된 다 .

Speech act, Speech event = ¢

A speech act is “doing something” with words. Thus, when someone says I
promise to be true, the utterance is the promise. Most speech acts are not as
direct as that, and their purpose (or illocutionary force) has to be inferred.

Substitution i %

Substitution is the replacing of a noun phrase or a whole clause by a single word.
This is done in order to avoid repetition, or to make a text more cohesive. For
example, in the sentence I don't really know what a gorgon is like, but I am quite
sure that Lady Smith is one, the word one substitutes for a gorgon.

Suggestopedia 암 시 교 수 범

Suggestopedia 15 3 method that applies principles of suggestion to teaching.
According to this method, the human mind is highly suggestible and capable of
prodigious feats of learning. In order to tap into this potential, the learner needs

to be eliminated—by 3 process of what is called de-suggestion.

Syllabus z+2%
A syllabus is an item-by-item description 아 016 teaching content of a course. On
the basis of the syllabus, a timetable or scheme of work can be drawn up. The

syllabus content helps specify what should be tested.

Task 과제

A task is a classroom activity whose focus is on communicating meaning. The
objective of a task may be to reach some consensus on an issue, to solve a
problem, to draft a plan, to design something, or to persuade someone to do
something. In contrast, practicing a pre-selected item of language for its own
sake would not be a valid task objective. In the performance of the tasks may
be receptive or productive, and may be done individually or in pairs or small

groups.

과 제 는 의 사 소 통 과 언 어 의 의 미 에 1 차 적 인 목 적 을 두 고 실 시 되 는 교 실 활 동 중 의 하 나 이 다 . 이는 미 리 선 택 된
언어 요 소 ( 형 태 ) 를 연 습 하 는 연 습 활 동 과는 차 이 가 있 다 . 139 68560 163「709 을 구 성 하 는 1235 는 정 해 진 답 을
의 사 소 통 을 통 해 찾 아 나 가 는 00569 tasket 정 해 진 해 결 책이 없 이 학 생 들 스 스 로 의 해 결 책 을 강 구 하 는 0067
1356 로 LHeICh

Task-based learning =71t &5

Task-based learning (TBL) is an approach that makes the task the basic unit
for planning and teaching. This contrasts with approaches that are centered
on grammar. The rationale underlying TBL originated in the communicative
approach, particularly in what is known as its strong version. Proponents of this
view argue that learning a language by using it. This contrasts with the weak
version: learning a language in order to use it. TBL share many of the principles

and practices of whole language learning.

과 제 기반 수 업 은 의 사 소 통 적 언 어 교 수 법 에 서 발 전 된 것 으 로 후 자 가 지 나 치 게 의 미 에 만 초 점 을 두 자 언 어 의

Teacher talk is the term used 10 describe the variety 아 language used by teachers

teachers interact with their learners by providing a source of input as well as

7[6>[ 텍 스 트

A text is 3 continuous piece of spoken or written language. It normally consists
of a number of linked sentences, and has a distinctive internal structure and
an identifiable communicative function. On the basis of their structure and
function, texts are classified into text types or genres. While texts are not as rule-
bound as sentences, there is the expectation that they will be coherent. There is
therefore some kind of logic that determines which sentences can go in which
order. Moreover, there are a number of ways that the sentences are seen to be

connected.

Total physical response 전신 반 응 교 수 법

Total Physical Response (TPR) 18 3 language-teaching method that is a
comprehension approach, based on the belief that learners need only understand
input, and should not be required to speak until they are ready to. TPR is
modeled on the way that young children receive comprehensible input in their
first language. Learners are exposed to input in the form of commands that

require a physical response, such as stand up, pick up the book, etc.

Transfer 전이

Language transfer is the effect that on language—particularly 016 first language—
has on another. It used to be known as interference, since, according to the
behaviorist view all transfer was seen as being negative. Thus learners’ errors
were attributed to the effect of first language habits transferred into the second.
Contrastive analysis of the L1 and the L2 attempted to predict and pre-empt such
errors. It became clear that transfer could also be positive as well as negative.
Where forms in the L1 match L2 forms, they can be borrowed successfully. In
fact, deliberate transfer from the Ls has been identified as a useful communication

strategy, especially if the L1 and the L2 share many features in common.

이 현 상 은 제 2 언 어 습 득 에 다 른 언 어 가 영 향 을 끼 치 는 현 상 으 로 특 히 모 국 어 의 전 이 현 상 을 가 리 킨 다 .
이 현 상 은 모 국 어 의 간 섭 현 상 인 interlingual transfer, 목 표 어 자 체 에 서 오 는 전 이 현 상인 730949 transfer?t

Universal Grammar (UG) ==

Universal grammar is the name given to the theory that all languages share
certain fundamental principles. The term was adopted by Noam Chomsky in
order to argue that we are genetically “programmed” with an innate language
learning faculty (sometimes called the language acquisition device or LAD).
UG describes the basic set of abstract principles that this biological mechanism
is thought to contain. These universal principles are adjusted for individual
languages according to choices that are governed by what are called parameters.

Uptake 흡 수

Uptake 16 what learners 16001 to have learnt from 3 language lesson. Typically
what learners say they have learnt does not necessarily match what the teacher
intended to teach. Moreover, uptake can vary from learner to learner. Factors that
appear to enhance uptake are salience, i.e., how much emphasis was given to an

item or topic.

Variability 변 이성

Variability is a characteristic of learners’ interlanguage. Learners often use more
than one way of expressing the same idea, more or less interchangeably. The
variability may be systematic or it may be free. Systematic variability occurs when
one choice is preferred to another in certain conditions, such as when the learner
is being more careful. However, some variability appears to be random and
unsystematic, ie, free. This supports the belief that the learner’s interlanguage 15

inherently unstable and in a constant state of flux.

를 발 화 하 기 도 하 는 특 성 을 말 한 다 , 변 이 성 을 지 니 는 오 류는 무 작 위 의 오 류 일 수 도 ,

Whole language learning 층 처 적 언어 교 수

Whole language learning 15 an educational approach to the teaching of literacy.
Its guiding principle is that language skills are best learned in authentic,

330 Build-up 영 어 교 육 론 |

## Page 331

Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @ F

meaningful situations. This contrasts with approaches which break language
up into discrete items or which separate it into different skills or competencies.
In focusing on language in its entirety, whole language learning is a holistic
approach, and adopts an integrated approach to the teaching of skills. This whole
language movement has strong parallels with task-based learning, content-based

learning, and immersion.

Young learner teaching

Research into the optimal age for learning a second language is still inconclusive.
While some researchers argue that the sooner the learner starts the better, others
are of the opinion that the disadvantages outweigh the benefits. Moreover,
learners who start later soon catch up. The special characteristics of young
learners, and those that distinguish them from adult learners, can be grouped

under the headings cognitive, affective, and social.

For a long time, up to the 16th century, English had been considered
inferior to Latin and not equal to expressing abstract and complex thoughts.
It took time for English to establish itself as a recognized medium. It
needed to establish a regular and uniform orthographical system and
to expand its vocabulary to meet the increased demands caused by the
demise of Latin and by developments in science and new discoveries
throughout the burgeoning Empire. From the 16th century onwards,
English flourished. A large number of classical works were translated into
English. They became available to the monolingual middle classes and
non-academics in general. William Wyclif's campaign against the 456 of
Latin by the church during the Protestant Reformation did much to assist
the establishment of English as the accepted form of communication
in all fields. Moreover, given the more widespread use of the printing
press, it rapidly became obvious that English-language books sold
better, so that market forces (a modern term applicable to this period)
did much to strengthen the position of English.

11. 8630 the following and answer the question.

Acupuncture techniques used in Asia as daily remedies over a
long history have now become distant to the general public. A major
reason why acupuncture is not widely understood is that it does not
demonstrate direct healing effects. An acupuncture needle is just a thin
piece of stainless steel without pharmacological properties. Analyzing
acupuncture in this way, however, cannot explain its treatment effects.
Within an oriental medicine perspective, the acupuncture needle itself
does not do the healing—it functions only as a key to activate the
healing process of the body. The brain is connected to sensors all
over the body, which manage its natural healing processes. When the
appropriate signal is received at certain places, the brain initiates healing
mechanisms, mostly controlled by hormones. The sensor locations are
called response points or acupuncture points. They are gates on our
bodies through which energy comes and goes; they also function as
energy storage and distribution points. Acupuncture functions as more
than just a purely physical input.

Which of the following would be the best title of the passage?

@ The Flow of Energy in 6 Body

® Acupuncture and Modern Medicine

@ The Proper Use of the Acupuncture Needle
® The Healing Process of Acupuncture

15, Read <A> and <B> and follow the directions.

After reading a story, the students build a mind map of the story
in a post-reading group activity. Students discuss the content of the
story first and then go on-line to create mind maps using a computer
program. This program provides templates to help build thoughts and
information using pictures, images, words and multimedia.

Here is an example of the template:

.
~. <5
~. <,

¥ heres

®

P
1

How to use this template:

1. Type the title of the story in the symbol labeled ‘STORY TITLE.’

2. Type appropriate information about characterization, themes and so
forth into the subsymbols.

3. Add symbols to further explain your ideas using the Create tool box.

B

a. This activity requires a bottom-up processing of input for reading.

transcript of two native speakers of English doing the same speaking
activity they just completed. Individually, the students read the transcript
and underline 311 the phrases that are used by the native speakers to
express ‘likes’and ‘dislikes’of school subjects. The teacher then reviews
these with the students. Following this, the teacher has the students find
all the examples of comparatives and superlatives in the transcript and
figure out how they differ in usage.

A

(1) Students actively monitor their comprehension processes when

reports are often used as a method of getting at the mental processes

options for responding to texts.

29. Read the following and answer the question.

Compare the two sets of sentences in (1) and (2).

(1) a. John was said to have solved all of the questions.
b. John was told to solve all of the questions.

(2) a. The earthquake was said to have hit the city.
b. *The earthquake was told to hit the city.
(The sentence with an asterisk ‘ * ” is unacceptable.)

The two sentences in (1) contain an NP-movement; an NP moves from
the position after the main verb to the subject position. The subject can
66 interpreted 35 identical with that of to-infinitive. We may assume
that the verb say and tell take the same type of complement. This
assumption, however, cannot be tenable because of the contrast shown
in (2). The contrast indicates that the subject in (2a) is not selected by
the verb say, while that in (2b) must be selected by the verb tell.

Here are some more examples whose structure is identical either with
(la)-type construction or with (1b)-type construction 35 discussed above.

a. The gladiators were supposed to survive brutal fights.

b. The passengers were reminded to fasten their seat belts.

c. The Amish people are reported to live and dress very simply.

d. The company’s workers were found to have organized a union.

e. The flood victims were advised to prepare food in hygienic conditions.
f. The listeners were invited to see the world in a different perspective.

30. Read the following and answer the question. [1.5%]

Lesson Procedure:

(1) The teacher shows the students postcards from many different
countries and introduces the activity by talking about the postcards
that people send to their friends when they are on vacation.

(2) The teacher asks the students about the postcards they have sent
home since arriving in the US: Who they have sent these to, what
kinds of messages they have written on them, and what cultural
aspects they have noticed on the postcards.

(3) The teacher has students form pairs. The teacher gives a prepared
postcard to one student in each pair. Student A, who receives a
postcard, describes it to Student B, who cannot see the postcard.
Student B then attempts to discover the identity of the country on the
postcard.

(4) Once all the students have completed the task, they share their
postcards and try to identify the culture-related aspects depicted on
the postcards with the rest of the class.

(5) The teacher focuses on some aspects related 10 American culture
and organizes these on the blackboard. The students discuss and
compare them with their own cultures.

(6) As 3 follow-up assignment, 6 students are asked to bring 10
postcards from their countries. They are asked 10 write 3 brief
paragraph about their own cultures.

32. Read <A> and <B> and follow the directions. [2.5%]

A

A phrase consists 이 3 head and non-head elements. Some non-head |

elements complete the meaning of the head. These elements are
referred to as a complement. It is a general term to denote any element
whose presence is required by the head. Although the presence of a
complement is normally obligatory, that of an N can be omitted. There |
are also elements in a phrase which describe the head rather than ː
complete it. These elements 316 modifiers (or adjuncts). They can be `
omitted without affecting grammaticality. |

B

An example of error in popular views @ about the mind appears
in the idea of a faculty of observation. One often hears it said that
we should train the observation ® of our students; and it is imagined
that by training them to observe certain things we are training them
to observe anything and everything. Observation, however, relies on
interest and knowledge. We have no reason to suppose that a botanist,
trained in the observation © of flowers, will be more observant than
us @ of the faces of the people he meets. People are more likely to
have their attention diverted (6) by the objects of their special interests.

50 training in the careful observation of the varied endings ® of Latin
words, or of the changes in chemical substances in experiments, will have
no effect on the observation of pictures or the movements of the stars.

in <B>.

34, Read <A> and <B> and follow the directions. [2.5%]

A

The following rules describe some characteristic features of Standard
American English.

(&)}

The lateral /1/ can be syllabic (i.e. standing 35 the nucleus of a
syllable) following a sequence of a stressed vowel and an alveolar stop
(an oral or a nasal stop).

(2)

A word-final /t/, /d/ or /n/ may assimilate in place of articulation to
a following word-initial bilabial or velar stop, resulting in two identical
consonants in some cases. But some features such as voicing and
nasality of the consonant remain constant. When place assimilation
results in two identical consonants, it is called total assimilation.

35. Read the following and answer the question. [1.5 점 ]

It has been argued that there are three kinds of speech acts: locutionary
act, illocutionary act, and perlocutionary act. A(n) (1)  actis
performed to convey the speaker’s intent 10 uttering 3 sentence (e.g.

| to praise, to criticize, 10 warn, to threaten, etc.). In the dialogue below,
the speaker can express his/her intention in the given situation without
manifesting it literally.

W ; Isn’t it too cold 10 here?

M : (Near a stove) I'll turn on the stove.
W : Thank you.

M : A pleasure of mine.

Information that is conveyed implicitly in a conversation is referred
to as conversational implicature. This can be accounted for in terms
of a conversational principle called the Co-operative Principle. In relation
to this principle, there are maxims assumed to ensure the facilitation 아
conversational interactions between hearer and speaker: the maxim of
quantity, the maxim of quality, the maxim of relation, and the maxim of
manner. 10 the above dialogue 6 woman didn’t make a request explicitly,
but the man understood her words as a request and turned on the stove.
How this was possible can be accounted for in terms of the maxim of

@)

with a problem or obstacle of some sort, is to act — either to take charge
themselves or to light a fire under someone else. They respond in this way
because they believe that doing something can make a difference. They are
an activist culture. Natasha lives in 3 different universe; she believes that the
individual is limited in what he or she can do, that many obstacles are truly
insurmountable, and there is, therefore, no point in doing something when
elevators break down. When such a person confronts a broken elevator,
her first impulse may very well be to just wait and see what happens next.
The goal is to endure.

My mistress’ eyes 316 nothing like the sun;

But no such roses 566 I in her cheeks;

And in some perfumes is there more delight

That music hath a far more pleasing sound;

My mistress, when she walks, treads on the ground.

As any she belied with false compare.

Commentary

Tone reflects the writer’s attitude toward 3 topic. It is the emotional
message behind the writer's words. Tone is chiefly controlled by the words
the writer chooses, words that color ideas, evoke desired emotions, and
imply judgments. The speaker in this poem draws a contrast between
the qualities often praised in exaggerated love poetry and the actuality
야 his mistress’physical attributes. After constructing 3 series of ‘false
comparisons’that this poem implies that other poets have used, the tone

39. Read the following and answer the question.

Up to the age of five I enjoyed the privileges of myopia, seeing the
world in a glorious haze like an impressionist painting. My contemporaries
appeared obscure and attractive, grown-ups loomed in vague magnificence.
I went daily to school and kept my eyes politely on the blackboard where
I could see only chalky confusion. After a year of this my mother noticed
that my education was at a standstill and sent me to the oculist: The world
sprang at me in hideous reality, full of people with open pores, blackheads
and impetigo. A deep-focus moustache appeared on an art mistress whom
I had considered beautiful. Flinching from this unusual clarity I went to
school and sat in my usual place at the morning assembly, unrecognizable
in a nose-pinching pair of wire-framed specs. The headmaster, whose
awareness of his pupils was always somewhat vague, thought that this
bespectacled intruder was 3 new boy. As I was too shy to disillusion him,
I was put back in the bottom class to restart my unpromising academic
career. I suppose I had become 3 new person, one who looked on 116
and actually saw it; but when faced with anything I am really reluctant
to see, like an animal killed and plastered 301055 the road, I still have the
defence of taking off my glasses and returning the world to the safe blur of
childhood.

09. Read the following and answer the question.

There are two words whose meanings reflect our somewhat warped
attitudes toward levels of commitment to physical and mental activities.
These are the terms amateur and dilettante. Nowadays, these labels are
slightly (1) . An amateur or a dilettante is someone not quite up to
par, a person not to be taken very seriously, one whose performance
falls short of professional standards. But originally, “amateur,” from the
Latin verb amare, “to love,” referred to a person who loved what he
was doing. Similarly, a “dilettante,” from the Latin delectare, “to find
delight in,” was someone who enjoyed a given activity. The earliest
meanings of these words therefore drew attention to experiences rather
than ~ (2) . They described the subjective rewards individuals gained
from doing things, instead of focusing on how well they were achieving.
Nothing illustrates as clearly our changing attitudes toward the value of
experience as the fate of these two words. There was a time when it
was admirable to be an amateur poet or a dilettante scientist, because
it meant that the quality of life could be improved by engaging in such
activities. But increasingly the emphasis has been to value behavior over
__(3)  states; what IS admired is success, achievement, the quality of
performance rather than the quality of experience.

10. Read the following and answer the question.

Society regards as true the systems of classification that produce the
desired results. The scientific test of “truth,” like the social test, is strictly
practical, except for the fact that the desired results are more severely
limited. The results desired by society may be irrational, superstitious,
selfish, or humane, but the results desired by scientists arc only that
our systems of classification produce predictable results. Classifications
determine our attitudes and behavior toward the object or event
classified. When lightning was classified as “evidence of divine wrath,”
no courses of action other than prayer were suggested to prevent
one’s being struck by lightning. But after Benjamin Franklin classified
it as “electricity,” a measure of control over it was achieved by the
invention of the lightning rod. Certain physical disorders were formerly
classified as “demonic possession,” and this suggested that we “drive
the demons out” by whatever spells and incantations we could think of.
The results were uncertain. But when those disorders were classified as
“bacillus infections,” courses of action were suggested that led to more
predictable results. Science seeks only the most generally useful systems
of classification; these it regards for the time being, until more useful

classifications are invented, as “true.”

Which of the following would be the best title of this passage?

@ The Importance of Societal Classification

@ The Eternity of Scientific Classification

® The Methodology 아 Effective Classification

@ The Implications of Different Classification Systems
® Societal Classification 35 3 Measure of Predictability

11. Read the following and answer the question.

Like the corporate pursuit of computer technology, profit-motivated
biotechnology creates several concerns. First is the concern that only
the rich will have access to such life-saving technologies as genetic
screening and cloned organs. Such fears are justified, considering
that companies have been patenting human life. The obesity gene,
the premature aging gene, and the breast cancer gene, for example,
have already been patented. These patents result in gene monopolies,
which could lead to astronomical patient costs for genetic screening
and treatment. A biotechnology industry argues that such patents are
the only way to recoup research costs that, in turn, lead to further
innovations. The commercialization of technology causes several other
concerns, including issues of quality control and the tendency for
discoveries to remain closely guarded secrets rather than collaborative
efforts. In addition, industry involvement has made government
control more difficult because researchers depend less and less on
federal funding. Finally, although there is little doubt that profit acts
as a catalyst for some scientific discoveries, other less commercially
profitable but equally important projects may be ignored.

12. Read the following and answer the question.

Over the last decade or so, the central debate In the field of early-
childhood education has been between one group that favors what you
might call a pre-academic approach to pre-kindergarten and kindergarten
and another group that contends that the point of school in those early
years is not to prepare for academic study but to allow children to
explore the world, learn social skills and have free, unconstrained fun.
The pre-academic camp seemed to dominate the debate in the late
1990s, drawing on some emerging research that showed that children’s
abilities at the beginning of kindergarten were powerful predictors of
later success. If a child reached his 5th birthday well behind his peers
in measures of cognitive ability, this research showed, he would most
likely never catch up. The good news in the research was that if you
exposed struggling children to certain intensive reading and math
interventions 10 pre-kindergarten and kindergarten, when their minds were
still at their most pliable, you could significantly reduce Dr even eliminate
that lag. And so the answer, to many scholars and policy makers, was
clear: . More recently, though,

a backlash has been growing against the pre-academic approach among
educators and child psychologists who believe that kindergarten should be a
garden of delight, not a place of stress and distress.

13. 86630 the following and answer the question.

Leonardo da Vinci just became even more prolific. An analysis released
last month claims a small portrait once attributed to a 19th-century German
artist was actually painted by the Italian master around the year 1500. The
surprising revelation is but the latest in a series of cases in which “lost” pieces
아 artwork were rediscovered through art authentication. But how can experts
66 so sure that a specific painter is responsible for a work of art?

In the case of the Da Vinci painting, the authentication was based
on physical evidence. Using a high-resolution multispectral camera, a
Canadian forensic-art expert named Peter Paul Biro was able to identify a
faint fingerprint left on the canvas. The print was then matched to one on a
known Da Vinci painting hanging in Vatican City.

Absent compelling forensic evidence like a fingerprint, the authentication
process becomes a bit murkier. In the past, pieces of art have been certified
through the combination of factors, including brushstroke patterns and
analysis of the artist’s signature. A painting’s provenance, or its history
of ownership, is also important. Being able to trace a portrait back from
owner-to-owner over the course of centuries is no small feat, making it one
that often lends significant weight to 3 work’s legitimacy.

One recent high-profile case highlighting the difficulties in authenticating
a piece of art is a disputed Jackson Pollock painting, purchased for $5 by
an ex-trucker in a thrift store. Biro was also involved in that investigation,
matching a partial fingerprint on the canvas to a paint can used by Pollock.
Despite the forensic evidence, the art community has been reluctant
to certify the work because there 15 no record of the painting’s former

ownership.

Activity Procedure

(1) Ask students to listen to a five-minute lecture while jotting down

lecture using their notes.

students three minutes to revise their summary using all of their
notes.

(3) Ask students to listen to the lecture one last time while they write
down as many other main points of the lecture as possible. Then,
give students two minutes to make a final revision of their summary.

30. Read <A> and <B> and follow the directions.

A

Assimilation, one of the most common phonological processes, comes
in two types, One is place assimilation, in which the assimilated sound
becomes similar to the conditioning sound in terms of place. The other is
manner assimilation, where a sound takes on the manner of articulation
from an adjacent sound. In English, these two types of assimilation can be
found 10 the alternations of the negative prefix ‘in-,’ 35 shown below.

(1) / in + kouhisrent / — [inkouhiorent]
(2) / 10 + regjalor / — / irregjolor / — [irégjolor]

(Note: 10 (2), after assimilation, degemination occurs, i.e., the two identical
consonants are fused into one.)

B
3 / 10 + ladzikol/ ‘llogical’
6 / in + matjuar / ‘immature’
c. / 1 ㅁ + rezalu:t / ‘irresolute’

d. / 10 + gretotju:d / ‘ingratitude’
6 / 10 + karekt / ‘incorrect’
